# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Consumer Fetch Request to Record Processing Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a Kafka consumer fetch request is built, sent, and processed back into ConsumerRecords in apache/kafka. Find Java source files implementing: the Fetcher request builder, the network poll, the fetch response parsing, and the ConsumerRecords population.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the Kafka consumer fetch request to record processing chain. Here's a summary of what I traced:

## Chain Overview

The answer documents the complete flow from fetch request building through to ConsumerRecords population:

1. **Request Building** - `prepareFetchRequests()` and `createFetchRequest()` in AbstractFetch construct FetchRequest.Builder instances for each broker
2. **Network Sending** - `sendFetchesInternal()` sends requests via `ConsumerNetworkClient.send()`
3. **Network Polling** - `ConsumerNetworkClient.poll()` handles the actual network IO
4. **Response Processing** - `handleFetchSuccess()` parses FetchResponse and creates CompletedFetch objects
5. **Record Collection** - `FetchCollector.collectFetch()` processes buffered fetches
6. **Record Deserialization** - `CompletedFetch.fetchRecords()` and `parseRecord()` deserialize records into ConsumerRecord objects
7. **Final Assembly** - ConsumerRecords is created from the Fetch object

## Key Files Identified

- **AbstractFetch.java** - Core request building and response handling
- **Fetcher.java** - Classic consumer fetch implementation
- **FetchRequestManager.java** - Async consumer fetch request management
- **FetchCollector.java** - Record collection from completed fetches
- **CompletedFetch.java** - Individual record parsing and deserialization
- **ConsumerNetworkClient.java** - Network request/response handling
- **ConsumerRecords.java** - Final result container

The answer.json file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains all files, symbols, the processing chain, and detailed narrative explanations of each stage.

This could be due to the partition\n562:      *         awaiting validation or awaiting reset.\n563:      *     </li>\n564:      * </ul>\n565:      *\n566:      * For those reasons, a partition that was <em>previously</em> in a fetchable state might not <em>currently</em>\n567:      * be in a fetchable state.\n568:      * </p>\n569:      *\n570:      * <p>\n571:      * Here's why this is important\u2014in a production system, a given leader node serves as a leader for many partitions.\n572:      * From the client's perspective, it's possible that a node has a mix of both fetchable and unfetchable partitions.\n573:      * When the client determines which nodes to skip and which to fetch from, it's important that unfetchable\n574:      * partitions don't block fetchable partitions from being fetched.\n575:      * </p>\n576:      *\n577:      * <p>\n578:      * So, when it's determined that a buffered partition is not in a fetchable state, it should be skipped.\n579:      * Otherwise, its node would end up in the set of nodes with buffered data and no fetch would be requested.\n580:      * </p>\n581:      *\n582:      * @param partitions Buffered partitions\n583:      * @param currentTimeMs Current timestamp\n584:      *\n585:      * @return Set of zero or more IDs for leader nodes of buffered partitions\n586:      */\n587:     private Set<Integer> bufferedNodes(Set<TopicPartition> partitions, long currentTimeMs) {\n588:         Set<Integer> ids = new HashSet<>();\n589: \n590:         for (TopicPartition partition : partitions) {\n591:             if (!subscriptions.isFetchable(partition))\n592:                 continue;\n593: \n594:             SubscriptionState.FetchPosition position = positionForPartition(partition);\n595:             Optional<Node> nodeOpt = maybeNodeForPosition(partition, position, currentTimeMs);\n596:             nodeOpt.ifPresent(node -> ids.add(node.id()));\n597:         }\n598: \n599:         return ids;\n600:     }\n601: ",

Fetch Request Builder Stage:**\\nFor each node with partitions to fetch, AbstractFetch.createFetchRequest() (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AbstractFetch.java:301) creates a FetchRequest.Builder. The request is queued in the unsent requests queue and response futures with listeners are registered.\\n\\n**4. Network Sending Stage:**\\nFetcher.sendFetchesInternal() (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/Fetcher.java:184) sends the FetchRequest.Builder instances via ConsumerNetworkClient.send() (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerNetworkClient.java:107). The request is queued in the unsent requests queue and response futures with listeners are registered.\\n\\n**4. Network Polling Stage:**\\nThe actual network IO occurs when ConsumerNetworkClient.poll() (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerNetworkClient.java:243) is called, which delegates to the underlying KafkaClient to send requests over the network and receive FetchResponse objects from brokers.\\n\\n**5. Response Processing Stage:**\\nWhen a FetchResponse is received, AbstractFetch.handleFetchSuccess() (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AbstractFetch.java:150) is invoked. This method:\\n- Parses the FetchResponse using FetchSessionHandler to get the per-partition data\\n- Creates CompletedFetch objects for each partition from FetchResponseData.PartitionData\\n- Stores these CompletedFetch objects in the FetchBuffer\\n\\n**6. Record Collection Stage:**\\nFetchCollector.collectFetch() (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/FetchCollector.java:92) processes CompletedFetch objects from the FetchBuffer. For each CompletedFetch:\\n- It checks if the partition is assigned and fetchable\\n- Calls CompletedFetch.fetchRecords() (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CompletedFetch.java:252) to extract up to maxPollRecords ConsumerRecord objects\\n\\n**7. Record Deserialization Stage:**\\nCompletedFetch.fetchRecords() iterates through RecordBatch objects and calls CompletedFetch.parseRecord() (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CompletedFetch.java:307) for each record. This method:\\n- Extracts the key and value ByteBuffers from the record\\n- Deserializes the key using the configured key deserializer\\n- Deserializes the value using the configured value deserializer\\n- Creates a ConsumerRecord object with the topic, partition, offset, timestamp, headers, and deserialized key/value\\n\\n**8. Final Assembly Stage:**\\nThe ConsumerRecord objects are accumulated in a Fetch object (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/Fetch.java) which groups records by TopicPartition. Finally, in ClassicKafkaConsumer or AsyncKafkaConsumer, a ConsumerRecords object (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/ConsumerRecords.java) is created from the Fetch's records map and returned to the application.\\n\\nKey supporting components:\\n- FetchSessionHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/FetchSessionHandler.java) manages fetch sessions and tracks session state across requests\\n- FetchRequestManager (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/FetchRequestManager.java) in the newer async consumer provides an alternative implementation for the fetch request creation and polling\\n- FetchBuffer manages buffered CompletedFetch objects for efficient memory usage\\n- FetchMetricsManager tracks metrics like fetch latency and partition lag throughout the process\"\n}\n",
